<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_EOLPAGE10"><a name="eolPage11"><a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_EOLPAGE11"><a name="eolPage14"><a name="eolPage15"><a name="FIS_UNIDENTIFIED_TABLE_5"><a name="eolPage16"><a name="FIS_UNIDENTIFIED_TABLE_7"><a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_EOLPAGE17"><a name="eolPage21"><a name="FIS_UNIDENTIFIED_TABLE_10"><a name="FIS_UNIDENTIFIED_TABLE_11"><a name="FIS_BALANCE_SHEET_3">NOTES
TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS </a></a></a></a></a></a></a></a></a></a></a></a></a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">September 30, 2009</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE 1 &#160;ORGANIZATION AND NATURE OF BUSINESS</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Northern Oil and Gas, Inc. (the &#8220;Company,&#8221; &#8220;we,&#8221; &#8220;us,&#8221; &#8220;our&#8221; and words of similar import) is a growth-oriented independent energy company engaged in the acquisition, exploration, exploitation and development of oil and natural gas properties.&#160;&#160;Prior to March 20, 2007, our name was
&#8220;Kentex Petroleum, Inc.&#8221;&#160;&#160;The Company took its present form on March 20, 2007, when Kentex completed a so-called short-form merger with its wholly-owned subsidiary, Northern Oil and Gas, Inc. (&#8220;NOG&#8221;), a Nevada corporation engaged in the Company&#8217;s current business, in which NOG merged into Kentex and Kentex was the surviving entity.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s common stock trades on the American Stock Exchange under the symbol &#8220;NOG&#8221;.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company will continue to focus on projects in the oil and gas industry primarily based in the Rocky Mountains and specifically the Williston Basin Bakken Shale formation. The Company has begun to develop its substantial leasehold in the Bakken play and will continue to do so as well as target additional opportunities in emerging plays
utilizing its first mover leasing advantage.&#160;&#160;We participate on a heads up basis in the drilling of wells on our leasehold.&#160;&#160;We own working interest in wells, and do not lease land to operators.&#160;&#160;To this point we have participated only in wells operated by others but have a substantial inventory of high working interest locations that we have begun to develop.&#160;&#160;We believe the advantage gained by participating as a non-operating partner in the over 100 gross oil wells completed
as of September 30, 2009 has given us valuable data on completions and will help our operating partners control well costs and enhance results as we continue to develop our higher working interest sections in 2009 and beyond.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company participates on a heads up basis proportionate to its working interest in a declared drilling unit.&#160;&#160;Although to this point we have participated with interests ranging from 1% to 51%, we expect to participate in incrementally higher working interest drilling units, eventually operating our inventory of high working
interest drilling units with a range of 40% to 100% ownership.&#160;&#160;We control approximately 70,000 net acres in the growing Williston Basin Bakken and Three Forks Play, which exposes us to approximately 110 net wells based on 640 acre spacing units and 220 net wells based on 320 acre spacing units.&#160;&#160;We believe recoveries from the Three Forks/Sanish formation&#160;&#160;and down spacing will potentially expose us to significantly more wells as development continues throughout the field.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Our land acquisition and field operations, along with various other services, are primarily outsourced through the use of consultants and drilling partners.&#160;&#160;The Company will continue to retain independent contractors to assist in operating and managing the prospects as well as to carry out the principal and necessary functions
incidental to the oil and gas business.&#160;&#160;With the additional acquisition of oil and natural gas properties, the Company intends to continue to use both in-house employees and outside consultants to develop and exploit its leasehold interests.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">As an independent oil and gas producer, the Company&#8217;s revenue, profitability and future rate of growth are substantially dependent on prevailing prices of natural gas and oil.&#160;&#160;Historically, the energy markets have been very volatile and it is likely that oil and gas prices will continue to be subject to wide fluctuations
in the future.&#160;&#160;A substantial or extended decline in natural gas and oil prices could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#8217;s financial position, results of operations, cash flows and access to capital, and on the quantities of natural gas and oil reserves that can be economically produced.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE 2 &#160;SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING PRACTICES</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FIS_UNIDENTIFIED_TABLE_3">The financial information included herein is unaudited, except the adjusted balance sheet as of December 31, 2008, which has been derived from our audited financial statements as of December 31, 2008.&#160;&#160;However, such information includes all adjustments (consisting solely of normal recurring adjustments),
which are in the opinion of management, necessary for a fair presentation of financial position, results of operations and cash flows for the interim periods.&#160;&#160;The results of operations for interim periods are not necessarily indicative of the results to be expected for an entire year. </a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">8</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Certain information, accounting policies, and footnote disclosures normally included in the financial statements prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America have been condensed or omitted in this Form 10-Q pursuant to certain rules and regulations of the Securities and Exchange Commission.&#160;&#160;The
financial statements should be read in conjunction with the audited financial statements for the year ended December 31, 2008, which were included in our Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended December 31, 2008 (also see Change in Accounting Principle Related to Drilling Costs below).</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_EOLPAGE9"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Cash, Cash Equivalents, and Short-Term Investments</font> </a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company considers highly liquid investments with insignificant interest rate risk and original maturities to the Company of three months or less to be cash equivalents.&#160;&#160;Cash equivalents consist primarily of interest-bearing bank accounts and money market funds.&#160;&#160;Our cash positions represent assets held in checking
and money market accounts.&#160;&#160;These assets are generally available to us on a daily or weekly basis and are highly liquid in nature.&#160;&#160;Due to the balances being greater than $250,000, we do not have FDIC coverage on the entire amount of bank deposits.&#160;&#160;The Company believes this risk is minimal.&#160;&#160;In addition, we are subject to SIPC protection on a vast majority of our financial assets.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Other Property and Equipment</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Property and equipment that are not oil and gas properties are recorded at cost and depreciated using the straight-line method over their estimated useful lives of three to five years.&#160;&#160;Expenditures for replacements, renewals, and betterments are capitalized.&#160;&#160;Maintenance and repairs are charged to operations as incurred.&#160;&#160;Long-lived
assets, other than oil and gas properties, are evaluated for impairment to determine if current circumstances and market conditions indicate the carrying amount may not be recoverable.&#160;&#160;We have not recognized any impairment losses on non oil and gas long-lived assets.&#160;&#160;Depreciation expense was $68,374 for the nine months ended September 30, 2009.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Debt Issuance Costs</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In February 2009, the Company entered into a revolving credit facility with CIT Capital USA, Inc. (CIT) (see Note 9).&#160; The Company incurred costs related to this facility that were capitalized on the Balance Sheet as Debt Issuance Costs.&#160; Included in the Debt Issuance Costs are direct costs paid to third parties for broker fees
and legal fees, 180,000 shares of restricted common stock paid as additional compensation for broker fees, and the fair value of 300,000 warrants issued to CIT.&#160; The fair value of the warrants was calculated using the Black-Sholes valuation model based on factors present at the time of closing.&#160; CIT can exercise these warrants at any time until the warrants expire in February 2012.&#160; The exercise price of the warrants is $5.00 per warrant.&#160; The total amount capitalized for Debt Issuance Costs
is $1,670,000.&#160; The capitalized costs will be amortized for three years over the term of the facility using the effective interest method.&#160;&#160;&#160;In May 2009, the Company amended the revolving credit facility with CIT to allow for additional borrowings.&#160;&#160;The Company incurred $216,414 of direct costs related to this amendment.&#160;&#160;The capitalized costs will be amortized over the remaining term of the facility using the effective interest method.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The amortization of debt issuance costs for the nine months ended September 30, 2009 was $312,386.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Asset Retirement Obligations</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company records the fair value of a liability for an asset retirement obligation in the period in which the asset is acquired and a corresponding increase in the carrying amount of the related long-lived asset.&#160;&#160;The liability is accreted to its present value each period, and the capitalized cost is depreciated over the useful
life of the related asset.&#160;&#160;If the liability is settled for an amount other than the recorded amount, a gain or loss is recognized.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Revenue Recognition and Gas Balancing</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">We recognize oil and gas revenues from our interests in producing wells when production is delivered to, and title has transferred to, the purchaser and to the extent the selling price is reasonably determinable.&#160;&#160;We use the sales method of accounting for gas balancing of gas production and would recognize a liability if the existing
proven reserves were not adequate to cover the current imbalance situation.&#160;&#160;As of September 30, 2009 and December 31,</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">9</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">2008, our gas production was in balance, i.e., our cumulative portion of gas production taken and sold from wells in which we have an interest equaled our entitled interest in gas production from those wells.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Stock-Based Compensation</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company has accounted for stock-based compensation under the provisions of FASB Accounting Standards Codification (ASC) 718-10-55 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 123(R), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Share-Based Payment).</font>&#8221;&#160;&#160;This
statement requires us to record an expense associated with the fair value of stock-based compensation.&#160;&#160;We currently use the Black-Scholes option valuation model to calculate stock based compensation at the date of grant.&#160;&#160;Option pricing models require the input of highly subjective assumptions, including the expected price volatility.&#160;&#160;Changes in these assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Income Taxes</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company accounts for income taxes under FASB ASC 740-10-30 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature, </font>FASB Statement 109, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting for Income Taxes)</font>.&#8221;&#160;&#160;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are determined based
upon differences between the financial reporting and tax bases of assets and liabilities and are measured using the enacted tax rates and laws that will be in effect when the differences are expected to reverse.&#160;&#160;Accounting standards require the consideration of a valuation allowance for deferred tax assets if it is &#8220;more likely than not&#8221; that some component or all of the benefits of deferred tax assets will not be realized.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_FORM10Q_05112009_HT"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Stock Issuance</font> </a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company records the stock-based compensation awards issued to non-employees and other external entities for goods and services at either the fair market value of the goods received or services rendered or the instruments issued in exchange for such services, whichever is more readily determinable, using the measurement date guidelines
enumerated in FASB ASC 505-50-30 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature, </font>EITF 96-18, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting for Equity Instruments That Are Issued to Other Than Employees for Acquiring or in Conjunction with Selling, Goods, or Services)</font>.&#8221;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Net Income (Loss) Per Common Share</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Basic earnings per share (EPS) is computed by dividing net income (the numerator) by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period (the denominator).&#160;&#160;Diluted EPS is computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares and potential common shares outstanding (if dilutive) during
each period.&#160;&#160;Potential common shares include stock options, warrants, and restricted stock.&#160;&#160;The number of potential common shares outstanding relating to stock options, warrants, and restricted stock is computed using the treasury stock method.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The reconciliation of the denominators used to calculate basic EPS and diluted EPS for the three and nine months ended September 30, 2009 and 2008 are as follows (in thousands):</font></div>

<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">10</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">s of September 30, 2009 there were 400,000 potentially dilutive shares from stock options that became exercisable in 2007.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In addition, as of September 30, 2009, there were 300,000 warrants that were issued in conjunction with the February 2009 revolving credit facility with CIT Capital USA, Inc. that remained outstanding and exercisable.&#160; These warrants are presently exercisable and represent potentially dilutive shares.&#160; Each of these warrants has
an exercise price of $5.00.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Full Cost Method</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company follows the full cost method of accounting for oil and gas operations whereby all costs related to the exploration and development of oil and gas properties are initially capitalized into a single cost center (&#8220;full cost pool&#8221;).&#160;&#160;Such costs include land acquisition costs, geological and geophysical expenses,
carrying charges on non-producing properties, costs of drilling directly related to acquisition, and exploration activities.&#160;&#160;Internal costs that are capitalized are directly attributable to acquisition, exploration and development activities and do not include costs related to the production, general corporate overhead or similar activities.&#160;&#160;Costs associated with production and general corporate activities are expensed in the period incurred.&#160;&#160;The Company capitalized $1,273,353
of internal costs and $456,398 of interest for the nine months ended September 30, 2009.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">As of September 30, 2009 we controlled acreage in Sheridan County, Montana with primary targets including the Red River and Mission&#160;Canyon. We controlled acreage in North Dakota, primarily in Mountrail&#160;County, targeting the Bakken Shale and Three Forks/Sanish as well as acreage in Yates County, New York that is prospective for
Marcellus Shale and Trenton-Black&#160;River natural gas production. Proceeds from property sales will generally be credited to the full cost pool, with no gain or loss recognized, unless such a sale would significantly alter the relationship between capitalized costs and the proved reserves attributable to these costs.&#160;&#160;A significant alteration would typically involve a sale of 25% or more of the proved reserves related to a single full cost pool.&#160;&#160;In the year ended December 31, 2008, the
Company sold acreage for $468,609.&#160;&#160;The proceeds for these sales were applied to reduce the capitalized costs of oil and gas properties. There were no property sales for the nine months ended September 30, 2009.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Capitalized costs associated with impaired properties and capitalized cost related to properties having proved reserves, plus the estimated future development costs, asset retirement costs under FASB ASC 410-20-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature:, </font>FASB Statement 143, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting
for Asset Retirement Obligations)</font> are depleted and amortized on the unit-of-production method based on the estimated gross proved reserves as determined by independent petroleum engineers.&#160;&#160;The costs of unproved properties are withheld from the depletion base until such time as they are either developed or abandoned.&#160;&#160;When proved reserves are assigned or the property is considered to be impaired, the cost of the property or the amount of the impairment is added to costs subject to depletion
calculations.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Capitalized costs of oil and gas properties (net of related deferred income taxes) may not exceed an amount equal to the present value, discounted at 10% per annum, of the estimated future net cash flows from proved oil and gas reserves plus the cost of unevaluated properties (adjusted for related income tax effects).&#160;&#160;Should
capitalized costs exceed this ceiling, impairment is recognized.&#160;&#160;The present value of estimated future net cash flows is computed by applying period-end prices of oil and natural gas to estimated future production of proved oil and gas reserves as of period-end, less estimated future expenditures to be incurred in developing and producing the proved reserves and assuming continuation of existing economic conditions.&#160;&#160;Such present value of proved reserves&#8217; future net cash flows excludes
future cash outflows associated with settling asset retirement obligations that have been accrued on the Balance Sheet (following SEC Staff Accounting Bulletin No. 106).&#160;&#160;Should this comparison indicate an excess carrying value, the excess is charged to earnings as an impairment expense.&#160;To this point the Company has not <a name="eolPage12">realized any impairment of its properties due to our low basis in the acreage and productivity and economics of our producing wells.&#160; </a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Use of Estimates</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The preparation of financial statements under generally accepted accounting principles (&#8220;GAAP&#8221;) in the United States requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and
the reported</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">11</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period.&#160;&#160;The most significant estimates relate to proved oil and natural gas reserve volumes, future development costs, estimates relating to certain oil and natural gas revenues and expenses, and deferred income taxes.&#160;&#160;Actual results may differ from those estimates.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Derivative Instruments and Price Risk Management</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company uses derivative instruments from time to time to manage market risks resulting from fluctuations in the prices of oil and natural gas.&#160;&#160;The Company may periodically enter into derivative contracts, including price swaps, caps and floors, which require payments to (or receipts from) counterparties based on the differential
between a fixed price and a variable price for a fixed quantity of oil or natural gas without the exchange of underlying volumes.&#160;&#160;The notional amounts of these financial instruments would be based on expected production from existing wells.&#160;&#160;The Company has, and continues to use exchange traded futures contracts and option contracts to hedge the delivery price of oil at a future date.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Derivatives are recorded on the balance sheet at fair value and changes in the fair value of derivatives are recorded each period in current earnings or other comprehensive income, depending on whether a derivative is designated as part of a hedge transaction and, if it is, depending on the type of hedge transaction.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s
derivatives consist primarily of cash flow hedge transactions in which the Company is hedging the variability of cash flows related to a forecasted&#160;transaction.&#160;&#160;Period to period changes in the fair value of derivative instruments designated as cash flow hedges are reported in other comprehensive income and reclassified to earnings in the periods in which the contracts are settled.&#160;&#160;The ineffective portion of the cash flow hedges is recognized in current period earnings as income or loss
from derivative.&#160;&#160;Gains and losses on derivative instruments that do not qualify for hedge accounting are included in income or loss from derivative in the period in which they occur.&#160;&#160;The resulting cash flows from derivatives are reported as cash flows from operating activities.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">At the inception of a derivative contract or upon identification of hedged production to which a derivative contract applies, the Company may designate the derivative as a cash flow hedge.&#160;&#160;For all derivatives designated as cash flow hedges, the Company formally documents the relationship between the derivative contract and the
hedged items, as well as the risk management objective for entering into the derivative contract.&#160;&#160;To be designated as a cash flow hedge transaction, the relationship between the derivative and the hedged items must be highly effective in achieving the offset of changes in cash flows attributable to the risk both at the inception of the derivative and on an ongoing basis.&#160;&#160;The Company measures hedge effectiveness on a quarterly basis and hedge accounting is discontinued prospectively if it
is determined that the derivative is no longer effective in offsetting changes in the cash flows of the hedged item.&#160;&#160;Gains and losses deferred in accumulated other comprehensive income related to cash flow hedge derivatives that become ineffective remain unchanged until the related production is delivered.&#160;&#160;If the Company determines that it is probable that a hedged forecasted transaction will not occur, deferred gains or losses on the derivative are recognized in earnings immediately.&#160;&#160;See
Note 14 for a description of the derivative contracts which the Company executed during 2009.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Impairment</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">FASB ASC 360-10-15 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature, </font>FASB Statement 144, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting for the Impairment and Disposal of Long-Lived Assets)</font> requires that long-lived assets to be held and used be reviewed for impairment whenever
events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable.&#160;&#160;Oil and gas properties accounted for using the full cost method of accounting (which we use) are excluded from this requirement but continue to be subject to the full cost method&#8217;s impairment rules.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Change in Accounting Principle Related to Drilling Costs</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In the third quarter of 2009, the Company changed its method of accounting for drilling costs from the accrual of drilling costs at the time drilling commenced for a well to recording the costs when amounts are invoiced by operators.&#160;&#160;Recording drilling costs when the amounts are invoiced by operators is deemed preferable as it
better represents the Company&#8217;s actual drilling costs.&#160;&#160;The recording of drilling costs in this method also is consistent with other companies in the oil and gas industry.&#160;&#160;The change decreased Depletion Expense by $512,794, increased Income Tax Provision by $206,000, and increased Net Income by $306,794 or $0.01 per share on a diluted basis for the nine months ended September 30, 2009.&#160;&#160;The effect of the change on the three months ended September 30,</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">12</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">2009 was to decrease Depletion Expense by $261,870, increase Income Tax Provision by $105,000 and to Increase Net Income by $156,870 or $0.00 per share on a diluted basis.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">New Accounting Pronouncements</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_EOLPAGE12">In March 2008, the FASB issued FASB ASC 815-10-15 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature, </font>FASB Statement 161, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Disclosures About Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities).</font>&#160;&#160;FASB
ASC 815-10-15 is intended to improve financial reporting about derivative instruments and hedging activities by requiring enhanced disclosures to enable investors to better understand their effects on an entity's financial position, financial performance, and cash flows.&#160;&#160;FASB ASC 815-10-15 is effective for financial statements issued for fiscal years and interim periods beginning after November 15, 2008, with early application encouraged.&#160;&#160;Pursuant to the transition provisions of the Statement,
the Company adopted FASB ASC 815-10-15 on January&#160;1, 2009.&#160;&#160;The required disclosures are presented in Note 14 on a prospective basis. This Statement does not impact the financial results as it is disclosure-only in nature. </a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In April&#160;2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 270-10-05 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>APB 28-1, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Interim Disclosures About Fair Value of Financial Instruments)</font>. The FASB ASC 270-10-05 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior
authoritative literature: </font>APB 28-1, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Interim Disclosures About Fair Value of Financial Instruments)</font> amends FASB ASC 825-10-50 <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">(Prior</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">13</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 107, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Disclosures About Fair Value of Financial Instruments)</font> to require an entity to provide disclosures about fair value of financial instruments in interim financial information. This
FASB ASC 270-10-05 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>APB 28-1, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Interim Disclosures About Fair Value of Financial Instruments)</font> is to be applied prospectively and is effective for interim and annual periods ending after June&#160;15, 2009 with early adoption permitted for periods ending after March&#160;15, 2009. The required disclosures are presented in&#160;Note 12 on a prospective basis.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In February&#160;2008, the FASB issued FSP FASB ASC 820-10-55 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB FSP 157-2/Statement 157, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Effective Date of FASB Statement No. 157.)</font> FASB ASC 820-10-55 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior
authoritative literature: </font>FASB FSP 157-2/Statement 157, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Effective Date of FASB Statement No. 157) </font>delayed the effective date for all nonfinancial assets and nonfinancial liabilities, except those that are recognized or disclosed at fair value in the financial statements on a recurring basis (at least annually). The adoption of the provisions of FASB ASC 820-10-55 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB
FSP 157-2/Statement 157, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Effective Date of FASB Statement No. 157) </font>related to nonfinancial assets and nonfinancial liabilities on January&#160;1, 2009 did not have a material impact on the Financial Statements. See Note 12 for FASB ASC 820-10-55 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB FSP 157-2/Statement 157, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Effective Date of FASB Statement No. 157) </font>disclosures.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In April 2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 820-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 157-4, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Determining Fair Value When the Volume and Level of Activity for the Asset or Liability Have Significantly Decreased and Identifying
Transactions That Are Not Orderly)</font>.&#160;&#160;FASB ASC 820-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 157-4, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Determining Fair Value When the Volume and Level of Activity for the Asset or Liability Have Significantly Decreased and Identifying Transactions That Are Not Orderly) </font>provides additional guidance in estimating fair value), when the volume and level of transaction activity
for an asset or liability have significantly decreased in relation to normal market activity for the asset or liability.&#160;&#160;FASB ASC 820-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 157-4, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Determining Fair Value When the Volume and Level of Activity for the Asset or Liability Have Significantly Decreased and Identifying Transactions That Are Not Orderly)</font>also provides additional guidance
on circumstances that may indicate a transaction is not orderly.&#160;&#160;FASB ASC 820-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 157-4, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Determining Fair Value When the Volume and Level of Activity for the Asset or Liability Have Significantly Decreased and Identifying Transactions That Are Not Orderly) </font>is effective for interim periods ending after June 15, 2009, and the Company has adopted
its provisions during second quarter 2009.&#160;&#160;FASB ASC 820-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 157-4, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Determining Fair Value When the Volume and Level of Activity for the Asset or Liability Have Significantly Decreased and Identifying Transactions That Are Not Orderly)</font> did not have a significant impact on the Company&#8217;s financial position, results of operations, cash
flows, or disclosures for third quarter 2009.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In April&#160;2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 320-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB FSP 115-2/124-2, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Recognition and Presentation of Other-Than-Temporary Impairments)</font>. The guidance applies to investments in debt securities
for which other-than-temporary impairments may be recorded. If an entity&#8217;s management asserts that it does not have the intent to sell a debt security and it is more likely than not that it will not have to sell the security before recovery of its cost basis, then an entity may separate other-than-temporary impairments into two components: 1) the amount related to credit losses (recorded in earnings), and 2) all other amounts (recorded in other comprehensive income). This ASC is to be applied prospectively
and is effective for interim and annual periods ending after June&#160;15, 2009 with early adoption permitted for periods ending after March&#160;15, 2009. The adoption of the provisions of this ASC in the second quarter 2009 did not have a material impact on the Financial Statements.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June 2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 860-10-05 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 166, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Accounting for Transfers of Financial Assets)</font>. FASB ASC 860-10-05 is effective for fiscal years beginning after November 15,
2009. The Company is currently assessing the impact of FASB ASC 860-10-05 on its financial position and results of operations.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June 2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 810-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 167-Amendment to FIN 46(R), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Consolidation of Variable Entities)</font>. FASB ASC 810-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior
authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 167-Amendment to FIN 46(R), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Consolidation of Variable Entities)</font> eliminates the quantitative approach previously required for determining the primary beneficiary of a variable interest entity and requires a qualitative analysis to determine whether an enterprise&#8217;s variable interest gives it a controlling financial interest in a variable interest entity. FASB ASC 810-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior
authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 167-Amendment to FIN 46(R), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Consolidation of Variable Entities) </font>contains<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">&#160;</font>certain guidance for determining whether an</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">14</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">entity is a variable interest entity. This statement also requires ongoing reassessments of whether an enterprise is the primary beneficiary of a variable interest entity. FASB ASC 810-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 167-Amendment to FIN 46(R), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Consolidation
of Variable Entities) </font>will be effective as of the beginning of the Company&#8217;s 2010 fiscal year. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of the adoption of FASB ASC 810-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 167-Amendment to FIN 46(R), <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Consolidation of Variable Entities)</font>.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June 2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 105-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 168, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">The FASB Accounting Standards Codification and the Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles</font>). Under FASB ASC
105-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 168, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">The FASB Accounting Standards Codification and the Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles)</font>, the FASB Accounting Standards Codification <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 70%; VERTICAL-ALIGN: text-top">&#8482; </font>(the &#8220;Codification&#8221;) will become the exclusive source of authoritative U.S. generally accepted
accounting principles (&#8220;U.S. GAAP&#8221;) recognized by the FASB to be applied by nongovernmental entities. Rules and interpretive releases of the Securities and Exchange Commission (&#8220;SEC&#8221;) under authority of federal securities laws are also sources of authoritative GAAP for SEC registrants. The Codification will supersede all then-existing non-SEC accounting and reporting standards, with the exception of certain non-SEC accounting literature which will become nonauthoritative. FASB ASC 105-10-65
(<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 168, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">The FASB Accounting Standards Codification and the Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles) </font>is effective for the Company&#8217;s 2009 third fiscal quarter. The adoption of FASB ASC 105-10-65 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 168, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">The
FASB Accounting Standards Codification and the Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles) </font>will not have a material impact on the Company&#8217;s Financial Statements. All references to U.S. GAAP provided in the notes to the Financial Statements have been updated to conform to the Codification.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In May 2009, the FASB issued FASB ASC 855-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 165, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Subsequent Events)</font>. FASB ASC 855-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB
Statement 165, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Subsequent Events) </font>provides guidance on management&#8217;s assessment of subsequent events and incorporates this guidance into accounting literature. FASB ASC 855-10-25 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature: </font>FASB Statement 165, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Subsequent Events) </font>is effective prospectively for interim and annual periods ending after June 15, 2009. The
implementation of this standard did not have a material impact on the Company&#8217;s financial position and results of operations. The Company has evaluated subsequent events through October 26, 2009, the date of issuance of the Company&#8217;s financial position and results of operations.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE 3 &#160;SHORT-TERM INVESTMENTS</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">All marketable debt and equity securities that are included in short-term investments are considered available-for-sale and are carried at fair value.&#160;&#160;The unrealized gains and losses related to these securities are included in accumulated other comprehensive income (loss).&#160;&#160; When securities are sold, their cost is determined
based on the first-in first-out method.&#160;&#160;The realized gains and losses related to these securities are included in other income in the statements of operations.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">For the nine months ended September 30, 2009 there were no realized gains or losses recognized on the sale of investments.&#160;&#160;In November 2008 we received, in a settlement agreement from UBS AG (&#8220;UBS&#8221;), rights which allow</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">15</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">us to put back the auction rate securities at par value to UBS starting in June 2010.&#160;&#160;We expect to liquidate these investments at par no later than June 2010, in the meantime they continue to pay interest at various rates.&#160;&#160;Under the settlement agreement with UBS, we also have the ability to borrow up to 75% of the
loan-to-market value of eligible <a name="FORM10Q_07292009_HTM_EOLPAGE13">auction rate securities on a no-net cost basis.&#160;&#160;As of September 30, 2009, we have borrowed $838,397 under this agreement, with an additional $680,353 of borrowings available under the agreement.&#160; </a></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company reviews these investments on a quarterly basis to determine if it is probable that the Company will realize some portion of the unrealized loss in accordance with FASB ASC 320-10-35 (<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Prior authoritative literature, </font>FASB Statement 115, 115-1, and 124-1, <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">The
Meaning of Other-Than-Temporary Impairment and Its Application to Certain Investments)</font>.&#160;&#160;&#160;In determining if the difference between cost and estimated fair value of the auction rate securities was deemed either temporary or other-than-temporary impairment, the Company evaluated each type of short-term investment using a set of criteria including decline in value, duration of the decline, period until anticipated recovery, nature of investment, probability of recovery, financial condition
and near-term prospects of the issuer, the Company&#8217;s intent and ability to retain the investment, attributes of the decline in value, status with rating agencies, status of principal and interest payments and any other issues related to the underlying securities. The Company determined the decline in the fair values in all of the investments in the auction rate securities were temporary as of September 30, 2009, primarily based on estimated cash flows of the investments, the settlement agreement entered
into with UBS, and the Company&#8217;s ability and intent to hold such investments until settlement.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<td align="right" valign="bottom" width="9%" style="BORDER-BOTTOM: black 4px double">
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman">298,410</font></div></td>
<td align="left" valign="bottom" width="1%" style="PADDING-BOTTOM: 4px"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman">&#160; </font></td></tr></table></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE 5&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;OIL AND GAS PROPERTIES</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Acquisition</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<br>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div>
<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">16</font></div>
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2"></div></div>
<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div></div></div>
<br>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In May 2009, the Company entered into an exploration and development agreement with Slawson Exploration Company, Inc. (Slawson) pursuant to which the Company acquired certain North Dakota Bakken assets from Windsor Bakken LLC as part of a syndicate led by privately owned Slawson.&#160; Pursuant to the agreement, the Company purchased a
five percent (5.0%) interest of the undeveloped acreage, including approximately 60,000 net acres.&#160; The Company also acquired an additional nine percent (9%) interest in the existing well bores purchased from Windsor Bakken LLC, providing the Company an aggregate fourteen percent (14%) interest in the existing 59 gross Bakken and Three Forks well bores in North Dakota including approximately 1,200 barrels of oil production per day.&#160; In the transaction, the Company purchased approximately 300,000 barrels
of proven producing reserves as well as approximately 3,000 net undeveloped acres.&#160;&#160;The Company paid a total cost of $7,300,000 for the initial acquisition of acreage and well bore interests.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">
<br></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE 6 &#160;PREFERRED AND COMMON STOCK</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Company has neither authorized nor issued any shares of preferred stock.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In February 2009, the Company agreed to issue 92,000 shares of Common Stock to three employees of the company as compensation for their services.&#160;&#160;The employees are fully vested in the shares on the date of the grant.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the stock to be issued was $261,280 or $2.84 per share, the market value of a share
of common stock on the date the stock was obligated to be issued.&#160;&#160;The entire amount of this stock award was expensed in the nine months ended September 30, 2009.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">On February 27, 2009, the Company closed on a revolving credit facility with CIT Capital USA, Inc. (CIT).&#160;&#160;As part of obtaining this credit facility agreement the Company entered into an engagement with Cynergy Advisors, LLC (Cynergy).&#160;&#160;As part of the compensation for the work performed on obtaining the financing, Cynergy
received 180,000 shares of restricted Common Stock of the Company.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the restricted stock was $475,200 or $2.64 per share, the market value of a share of Common Stock on the date the financing closed.&#160;&#160;The fair value of this stock was capitalized as Debt Issuance Costs and is being amortized for three years over the term of the financing.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">On April 3, 2009 the Company acquired leasehold interests in North Dakota. The total consideration paid for this acreage was 49,092 shares of restricted common stock.&#160; The fair value of the restricted stock was $224,879, or $4.58 per share, the market value of a share of Common Stock on the date the leasehold interests were acquired.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June 2009, the Company completed a registered direct offering of 2,250,000 shares of common stock at a price of $6.00 per share for total gross proceeds of $13,500,000.&#160; C.K. Cooper &amp; Company acted as lead placement agent on the transaction for which it received consideration in cash.&#160;&#160;The Company incurred costs of
$813,237 related to this offering.&#160;&#160;These costs were netted against the proceeds of the offering through Additional Paid-In Capital.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Restricted Stock Awards</font></font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In March 2008, the Company issued 20,000 shares of restricted common stock to employee James Sankovitz pursuant to a written employment agreement.&#160;&#160;The issuance of restricted stock is intended to retain and motivate the employee.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the award was $140,500 or $7.03 per share, the average market value of
a share of Common Stock on the date the stock was issued. The fair value was expensed over the one-year term of the award.&#160;&#160;The Company expensed $35,125 related to this award in the nine months ended September 30, 2009.&#160;&#160;The shares are fully vested at September 30, 2009.&#160;&#160;Vesting of the shares was contingent on the employee maintaining employment with the Company and other restrictions included in the employment agreement.</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In February 2009, the Company granted 60,000 shares of restricted common stock to employees James Sankovitz and Chad Winter pursuant to written agreements.&#160;&#160;The grants of restricted stock are intended to retain and motivate the employees.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the awards was $170,400 or $2.84 per share, the market value
of a share of common stock on the date the stock was granted.&#160;&#160;30,000 of the shares become fully vested on January 1, 2010 and 30,000 of the shares become fully vested on January 1, 2011.&#160;&#160;The fair value will be expensed evenly over the term of the award.&#160;&#160;The Company expensed $87,763 related to those awards in the nine months ended September 30,</font></div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>
